(HCS) is a privately held behavioral health software company headquartered in Montgomery, Alabama. Founded in 1983 by a pharmacist and software engineer, HCS has over 40 years of experience delivering clinical software for healthcare facilities. The company specializes exclusively in **behavioral health** — serving psychiatric hospitals, residential treatment centers (RTCs), substance use disorder (SUD) programs, outpatient behavioral health organizations, and correctional healthcare facilities.\n     9→\n    10→HCS positions itself as a unified platform covering clinical, financial, operational, and compliance workflows. The company claims its software is used by \"thousands of clinicians and financial analysts\" nationwide. Their partner/customer list is notable — it includes major behavioral health hospital chains such as **Universal Health Services (UHS)**, **Acadia Healthcare**, **HCA Healthcare**, **LifePoint Behavioral Health**, **Haven Behavioral Healthcare**, **Summit BHC**, **National HealthCare Corporation**, **US Healthvest**, and **Malvern Health**. These are some of the largest operators of psychiatric hospitals and behavioral health facilities in the U.S., suggesting HCS has significant market penetration in the inpatient behavioral health segment. Technology/data exchange partners include **Surescripts** (e-prescribing), **Merative** (formerly IBM Watson Health / Truven — likely for analytics or data exchange), and **Hawaii Health Information Exchange**.\n    11→\n    12→The company is staffed in part by clinicians (\"We're Clinicians Too\") and emphasizes quick deployments (\"in weeks instead of months\"). HCS Cloud hosting is available. There is no indication of recent acquisitions or rebranding — the company appears to have operated under the same name since founding.\n    13→\n    14→## Product: HCS eMR (and broader HCS Behavioral Health Software Suite)\n    15→\n    16→CHPL ID: 11416\n    17→\n    18→### What It Is\n    19→\n    20→HCS eMR is a **comprehensive behavioral health electronic medical record system** designed for inpatient and residential behavioral health settings. The CHPL certification identifies the product as \"HCS eMR\" version 10 (certified December 2023), but in practice the certified module is part of a broader integrated suite that HCS markets as their \"Behavioral Health Software\" platform. The SED intended user description confirms this is for **\"Physicians, Nurses, Pharmacists and other Clinical Disciplines in an Inpatient Setting\"** with HIM (Health Information Management) users also included for the EHI export criterion (b)(11).\n    21→\n    22→The certification is very broad — 40+ criteria spanning clinical data (a)(1)–(a)(15), transitions of care (b)(1)–(b)(2), clinical information exchange (b)(7)–(b)(9), patient portal (e)(1), public health reporting (f)(1)–(f)(7), FHIR API (g)(10), and immunization/syndromic/reportable conditions exchange. This indicates a full-featured clinical EHR with pharmacy, CPOE, patient portal, and public health reporting capabilities.\n    23→\n    24→### Users & Market\n    25→\n    26→**Primary users**: Psychiatrists, nurses, pharmacists, therapists/counselors, HIM staff, billing/financial analysts, compliance officers, call center/intake coordinators, and practice administrators at behavioral health facilities.\n    27→\n    28→**Clinical settings**:\n    29→- Psychiatric hospitals (acute inpatient)\n    30→- Residential treatment centers (RTCs)\n    31→- Substance use disorder (SUD) treatment programs\n    32→- Partial hospitalization programs (PHP)\n    33→- Intensive outpatient programs (IOP)\n    34→- Outpatient behavioral health organizations\n    35→- Correctional healthcare facilities\n    36→- Crisis centers\n    37→\n    38→**Notable customers/partners**: Summit BHC (39+ locations nationwide, including Northern Path Recovery Center in Fort Wayne, IN as a documented deployment), Algani Consulting (multi-state behavioral health organization implementing the full HCS suite across all facilities), and the major chains listed above (UHS, Acadia, HCA, LifePoint, Haven, NHC, US Healthvest, Malvern).\n    39→\n    40→### Modules & Functionality\n    41→\n    42→HCS markets seven primary product areas, all integrated within the single platform. Based on vendor materials, press releases, and product pages:\n    43→\n    44→**1. Behavioral Record (Core Clinical EMR)**\n    45→- Patient intake and evaluation: collects personal details, medical history, assessments, symptoms, eligibility information\n    46→- Treatment planning: patient goals, objectives, interventions, expected outcomes; supports multiple diagnoses across behavioral and medical conditions\n    47→- Over 50 peer-reviewed behavioral health assessment tools including ASAM 4 (addiction severity), PHQ-9 (depression screening), and C-SSRS (suicide risk screening)\n    48→- Group therapy notes documentation\n    49→- Administrative and clinical bed board: real-time visibility into patient flow, bed availability, caseload, exam results, insurance status, risk management rules\n    50→- AIDA (Artificial Intelligence Dictation Assistant): ambient conversational listening with real-time speech-to-text, OpenAI-powered transcription, structured form fill, multi-language support\n    51→- Scheduling module for clinician, therapist, and patient appointments, therapy sessions, and activities\n    52→- Rules-based workflow engine monitoring time-restricted tasks with notifications\n    53→- Community Portal: patient-facing portal for scheduling, documentation completion, care record access, and provider communication (aligns with (e)(1) certification)\n    54→\n    55→**2. Call Center CRM**\n    56→- Pre-admission screening and expedited onboarding\n    57→- Referral management with quality documentation\n    58→- Patient engagement and alumni tracking\n    59→- Treatment coordination and follow-up reminders\n    60→- Reporting and analytics\n    61→\n    62→**3. Revenue Cycle Management (Billing/Financial)**\n    63→- Electronic eligibility/insurance verification\n    64→- Automated charge capture from intake through discharge\n    65→- Claim workflow management (every claim tracked to zero balance)\n    66→- Denial prevention with proactive alerts before claim submission\n    67→- Electronic Remittance Advice (ERA) processing\n    68→- Billing reports integrated with HCS Analytics\n    69→- Insurance verification, charge documentation, claim processing, payment tracking, denial management\n    70→\n    71→**4. Order Management (CPOE)**\n    72→- Computerized provider order entry for medications, labs, radiology, and tasks\n    73→- Integration with automated dispensing devices, pharmacy, laboratory, and radiology systems\n    74→\n    75→**5. Medication Management (eMAR, ePharmacy, MEDICS, MAT)**\n    76→- eMAR: Electronic Medication Administration Record with barcode scanning for unit dose labels; documented 33% reduction in medication errors and 45% reduction in documentation time\n    77→- Medication reconciliation with 12-month prescription history query (via Surescripts)\n    78→- Home-to-admission and discharge medication reconciliation\n    79→- ePrescribing for both controlled and non-controlled substances (EPCS)\n    80→- Medication Assisted Treatment (MAT) — specific module for SUD programs (e.g., buprenorphine, methadone protocols)\n    81→- HCS MEDICS: Pharmacy information system built on 30+ years of clinical experience, designed by pharmacists\n    82→- HCS ePharmacy: Medication order entry, verification, and clinical alerts documentation\n    83→- Clinical alerts, therapeutic substitution recommendations\n    84→- Visual alerts for medication due dates and overdue statuses\n    85→- Clinical status board for group medication monitoring\n    86→\n    87→**6. Patient Safety**\n    88→- Safety Checks (patented, US Patent #US11869638): Electronic observation rounding tool replacing paper-based processes; captures patient location, clinical status, and clinician location at configurable intervals (every 5, 15, 30, or 60 minutes)\n    89→- Quality minute rounding with proximity beacons\n    90→- Clinical decision support with intelligently derived problem lists and template-driven treatment planning\n    91→- Patient education documentation tracking comprehension of medications and treatments\n    92→- Safe patient hand-off protocols\n    93→\n    94→**7. Compliance Toolkit**\n    95→- Compliance Monitor tracking: unsigned orders/documents, time-based form compliance, Z code and ASAM analysis, readmission tracking, antibiotic stewardship, medication administration analysis, C-SSRS completion rates, discharge disposition, opioid administration oversight\n    96→- IPFQR (Inpatient Psychiatric Facility Quality Reporting) publication to CMS\n    97→- Credentialing Manager: primary source verification, license tracking, automated recertification reminders, provider/payor enrollment, network inclusion, privileging authorization\n    98→- Automated chart review\n    99→- Critical task notifications with intelligent escalation\n   100→- Metabolic screening measures\n   101→- Graphical reporting for HIPAA, billing/coding, regulatory, quality, security, and privacy\n   102→\n   103→**Cross-cutting capabilities**:\n   104→- Multi-factor authentication (barcode badge, Active Directory, tokenized verification for EPCS)\n   105→- Real-time data analytics (HCS Analytics)\n   106→- Cloud hosting (HCS Cloud)\n   107→- Telehealth video conferencing for remote therapy sessions\n   108→- Public health reporting: immunizations, syndromic surveillance, electronic case reporting, cancer registry, antimicrobial use/resistance (certified for (f)(1)–(f)(7))\n   109→- FHIR API access (certified for (g)(10))\n   110→- Transitions of care / C-CDA exchange (certified for (b)(1), (b)(2))\n   111→\n   112→### Data & Content\n   113→\n   114→Based on the certified criteria and vendor materials, HCS eMR stores/manages the following data a Demo Meaningful Use HCS eMR Real World Testing Real World Testing is a requirement outlined in the ONC 21st Century Cures Act Final Rule for all health IT developers participating in the ONC Health IT Certification Program . The purpose of this annual Condition and Maintenance of Certification requirement is for Certified Health IT Developers to demonstrate interoperability and functionality of their certified health IT in real world settings and scenarios, rather than in a controlled test environment with an ONC-Authorized Testing Lab. Real World Testing verifies that deployed Certified Health IT continues to perform as intended by conducting and measuring observations of interoperability and data exchange. 2025 Test Plan and Results 2024 Test Plan and Results 2023 Test Plan and Results 2022 Test Plan and Results &nbsp; HCS EHI Export This EHI Export Documentation is complete with all required elements and includes sufficient instruction to allow users to export either single patient or patient populations without HCS assistance and at no charge. Exports generated using the methodology outlined above will occur in real time and be in a compressed (ZIP) format containing CSV files with the actual EHI and a readme file with a hyperlink to the most up to date data dictionary for the file format. HCS will update the data dictionary as the database structure evolves with each new version. All information in this documentation is up to date and fully addresses the health IT developer’s EHI Export Requirements. EHI Export Instructions EHI Data Dictionary &nbsp; ONC Certification HCS eMR10 Certificate Developer organization name – Health Care Systems Date the product was certified – December 20, 2023 Product name and version &#8211; HCS eMR 10 Unique certification number &#8211; 15.99.04.1582.HC01.10.02.1.231220 Certification criteria to which the product has been certified &#8211; 170.315 (a)(1-5, 12, 14-15); (b)(1-2, 7-11); (c)(1-4); (d)(1-13); (e)(1, 3); (f)(1-7); (g)(2-7, 9-10); (h)(1) CQMs to which the product has been certified &#8211; 9v8, 71v9, 72v8, 104v8, 105v8, 108v8, 111v8, 190v8 Any additional software the certified product relied upon to demonstrate its compliance with certification criteria &#8211; IBM MicroMedex, EMR Direct Interoperability Engine ONC Disclaimer:  &#8220;This Health IT Module is compliant with the ONC Certification Criteria for Health IT and has been certified by an ONC-ACB in accordance with the applicable certification criteria adopted by the Secretary of Health and Human Services. This certification does not represent an endorsement by the U.S. Department of Health and Human Services.&#8221; Additional types of costs to users may be required to pay include one-time implementation fees, interface or integration fees (including those from third party vendors) and clinical content fees. HCS eMR utilizes multi-factor authentication (MFA) in a variety of ways to enable additional security around several key workflows. MFA can be enabled before log in using Active Directory connections into third party tools for digital verification on a secondary device or by using barcode technology to read an employee badge to verify the person logging in is who they say they are. Within the HCS Clinicals, MFA can be performed using barcode technology when performing actions that would normally require a signature (ordering or administering medications or signing documentation). MFA can also be performed using third party tools for tokenized verification for ePrescribing of Controlled Substances. HCS eMR uses the latest technologies to ensure our providers are properly credentialed before accessing, entering, or modifying your patient’s health information. a Demo Meaningful Use HCS eMR Real World Testing Real World Testing is a requirement outlined in the ONC 21st Century Cures Act Final Rule for all health IT developers participating in the ONC Health IT Certification Program . The purpose of this annual Condition and Maintenance of Certification requirement is for Certified Health IT Developers to demonstrate interoperability and functionality of their certified health IT in real world settings and scenarios, rather than in a controlled test environment with an ONC-Authorized Testing Lab. Real World Testing verifies that deployed Certified Health IT continues to perform as intended by conducting and measuring observations of interoperability and data exchange. 2025 Test Plan and Results 2024 Test Plan and Results 2023 Test Plan and Results 2022 Test Plan and Results &nbsp; HCS EHI Export This EHI Export Documentation is complete with all required elements and includes sufficient instruction to allow users to export either single patient or patient populations without HCS assistance and at no charge. Exports generated using the methodology outlined above will occur in real time and be in a compressed (ZIP) format containing CSV files with the actual EHI and a readme file with a hyperlink to the most up to date data dictionary for the file format. HCS will update the data dictionary as the database structure evolves with each new version. All information in this documentation is up to date and fully addresses the health IT developer’s EHI Export Requirements. EHI Export Instructions EHI Data Dictionary &nbsp; ONC Certification HCS eMR10 Certificate Developer organization name – Health Care Systems Date the product was certified – December 20, 2023 Product name and version &#8211; HCS eMR 10 Unique certification number &#8211; 15.99.04.1582.HC01.10.02.1.231220 Certification criteria to which the product has been certified &#8211; 170.315 (a)(1-5, 12, 14-15); (b)(1-2, 7-11); (c)(1-4); (d)(1-13); (e)(1, 3); (f)(1-7); (g)(2-7, 9-10); (h)(1) CQMs to which the product has been certified &#8211; 9v8, 71v9, 72v8, 104v8, 105v8, 108v8, 111v8, 190v8 Any additional software the certified product relied upon to demonstrate its compliance with certification criteria &#8211; IBM MicroMedex, EMR Direct Interoperability Engine ONC Disclaimer:  &#8220;This Health IT Module is compliant with the ONC Certification Criteria for Health IT and has been certified by an ONC-ACB in accordance with the applicable certification criteria adopted by the Secretary of Health and Human Services. This certification does not represent an endorsement by the U.S. Department of Health and Human Services.&#8221; Additional types of costs to users may be required to pay include one-time implementation fees, interface or integration fees (including those from third party vendors) and clinical content fees. HCS eMR utilizes multi-factor authentication (MFA) in a variety of ways to enable additional security around several key workflows. MFA can be enabled before log in using Active Directory connections into third party tools for digital verification on a secondary device or by using barcode technology to read an employee badge to verify the person logging in is who they say they are. Within the HCS Clinicals, MFA can be performed using barcode technology when performing actions that would normally require a signature (ordering or administering medications or signing documentation). MFA can also be performed using third party tools for tokenized verification for ePrescribing of Controlled Substances. HCS eMR uses the latest technologies to ensure our providers are properly credentialed before accessing, entering, or modifying your patient’s health information. EHI Export Instructions PDF (2 pages, scanned document)\n\nThe PDF is a scanned paper document (produced by a Konica Minolta bizhub C364e scanner on 2023-12-19), so text extraction yields nothing — the content is only in the page images.\n\n**Page 1** contains:\n- **Product identification**: HCS eMR v10.0\n- **Overview**: Describes a real-time export of all patient information stored in the EHR. The export is available without interacting with HCS Support or Developers. It produces a collection of comma-separated value (CSV) files and a readme file containing a hyperlink to the most up-to-date data dictionary. HCS maintains and updates this documentation as part of their release notes process.\n- **User Access**: The EHI Export function is configurable but defaults to availability for Corporate Users. The \"Corporate User\" authorization role is typically assigned to Administrators and Analysts for EHR at the organization. Organizations use Active Directory to maintain access. The functions are built into HCS eMR at no additional charge and are available autonomously.\n- **Instructions (Creating the Export)**: Users go to System→EHI Export. The menu/screen is the same Patient Selection tool used elsewhere in the application. Users can select a single patient by Visit Identifier, or a group of patients using various filter parameters. After selecting patient(s), users click \"View Patients\" to review the list, then \"Export Patients\" to perform the export.\n\n**Page 2** contains:\n- **Screenshot of the export interface**: Shows the \"Electronic Health Information Export\" screen with extensive filtering options including:\n  - Active in Date Range and Patient Set\n  - Active in Date Range\n  - Active in Patient Set\n  - All Currently Active\n  - Admit Date Range and Patient Set\n  - Admit Date Range\n  - Discharge Date Range and Patient Set\n  - Discharge Date Range\n  - Discharge Date Range and Assigned to Staff\n  - Discharge Date Range and Class\n  - Not Discharged Date Range and Class\n  - Patients with Address in Date Range\n  - Patients with Address in Date Range and Prescriber\n  - Any Entries in Date Range\n  - Patients with Entries in Date Range and Prescriber\n  - Patients with Entries in Date Range\n- **Instructions (Reading the Export)**: The ZIP file exported to the user's \"Downloads\" directory contains a CSV file for each table in the HCS database. The data dictionary describes the data type and size of each field, plus a description of how the field is used and how it relates to other tables. The data dictionary is provided in CSV format for machine readability.\n- **Key statement**: \"The files exported as part of the HCS EHI Export contain all necessary data, including that which is not strictly personal health information, to allow the creation of a complete and fully usable HCS database with only the patient(s) that the users chose to export.\"\n- **Attestation**: Signed by Reubin Felkey (Authorized Representative) on 12/18/2023, stating the documentation is complete with all required elements.\n\n### 2. EHI Data Dictionary CSV (339 tables, 3,878 columns)\n\nThe CSV file has five columns: `Table`, `Column`, `Type`, `Size`, `Description`. It documents every table and column in the HCS database that is included in the EHI export. Each table's first row has only the Table and Description fields filled. detail (credentials, NPI, DEA, specialties)\n- `StaffPractitionerID`, `StaffSpecialty`, `StaffIDCode` — provider identifiers\n\n**Safety and compliance:**\n- `VisitPhysicalLocation` (8 cols) — patient physical location tracking (proximity beacons for safety rounds)\n- `NearMiss` (11 cols) — near-miss safety events\n- `ClinicalAlert` (21 cols) — clinical alerts\n\n**Other notable tables:**\n- `VisitDocument` (19 cols) — visit-specific documents\n- `VisitNote` (7 cols) — clinical notes\n- `VisitInstruction` (14 cols) — discharge/care instructions\n- `VisitImmunizationQuery` (11 cols) — immunization queries\n- `VisitTransfer` (11 cols) — patient transfers between units\n- `VisitFlag` (5 cols) — patient flags/alerts\n- `ConsentDocument` (4 cols) — consent document storage\n- `Chat`/`ChatMessage` (messaging)\n- `Event`/`EventOccurrence` — scheduling/events\n\n## Export Coverage Assessment\n\n### Data Domain Coverage\n\nThis is an exceptionally thorough EHI export. HCS has taken the (b)(10) requirement seriously by exporting **the entire relational database structure** as CSV files — one per table — rather than limiting the export to a standardized clinical subset. The explicit statement in the instructions that the export contains \"all necessary data... to allow the creation of a complete and fully usable HCS database\" demonstrates genuine understanding of what a full EHI export means.\n\n**Clearly covered domains:**\n- **Demographics and patient identity**: Patient table with 37 columns including race, ethnicity, language, religion, marital status, veteran status, SSN, plus separate PatientAddress, PatientAlias, PatientContact, PatientIdentifier, PatientRace tables\n- **Clinical encounters/visits**: PatientVisit (48 cols) with admission, discharge, class, attending, location\n- **Diagnoses and problem lists**: VisitDiagnosis, VisitProblem, VisitProspectiveProblem, Condition tables\n- **Medications**: PatientOrder (143 cols — the most detailed table), full pharmacy product hierarchy (DispensableProduct, RoutedProduct, PackagedProduct, NamedProduct), medication reconciliation (MedRecItem), medication list (HCS_MedList)\n- **Medication administration**: TherapyAdmin (45 cols), AdminProduct, AdminVolume, AdminComponent, AdminField — detailed MAR data\n- **Allergies**: PatientAllergy (20 cols)\n- **Clinical observations/vitals/labs**: Observation (88 cols), ObservationGroup (62 cols), ObservationGroupItem (71 cols), VisitObservation (46 cols), VisitObservationSet (58 cols)\n- **Procedures**: VisitProcedure (18 cols)\n- **Devices**: PatientDevice (13 cols), DeviceIdentifier\n- **Clinical documents**: PatientDocument, VisitDocument, VisitNote\n- **Billing/charges**: VisitCharge (60 cols) with CPT, revenue codes, diagnosis pointers, amounts — genuinely detailed financial data\n- **Claims**: ChargeClaim (40 cols), PatientClaimResponse, ClaimObservation\n- **Insurance/coverage**: PatientInsuranceCoverage (27 cols), InsuranceCompany, InsuranceContract, VisitInsuranceCoverage, VisitInsuranceAuthorization, VisitEligibilityQuery\n- **Payments**: Payment (12 cols), CopayProduct, CopaySummary\n- **Treatment plans/interventions**: VisitIntervention (33 cols) with goals, objectives, outcomes — critical for behavioral health\n- **Care plans**: VisitCarePlan, VisitCareLevel, VisitConcern\n- **Consents**: PatientConsent (23 cols), VisitConsent, ConsentDocument\n- **Safety data**: VisitPhysicalLocation (patient location tracking), NearMiss\n- **Immunizations**: VisitImmunizationQuery, ImmunizationQueryForecast, ImmunizationQueryHistory\n- **Discharge instructions**: VisitInstruction (14 cols)\n- **Referrals/transfers**: VisitTransfer, VisitServiceLevel\n- **Family history**: PatientFamilyHistoryItem\n- **Clinical alerts**: ClinicalAlert (21 cols), ClinicalRelationship\n- **Pharmacy management**: PBM tables (formulary, coverage, copay), DispenseBatch, product substitution, interaction checking\n- **Scheduling/events**: Event, EventOccurrence, EventItem, CalendarDay\n- **Staff/provider data**: Staff (80 cols) — provider context needed to interpret clinical records\n\n**Behavioral health-specific coverage:**\nWhile the data dictionary doesn't have tables explicitly named for behavioral health assessments (e.g., no \"PHQ9\" or \"CSSRS\" table), the behavioral health assessment data is stored in the **Observation/ObservationGroup/ObservationGroupItem** hierarchy. The Observation table alone has 88 columns and includes coded values, numeric results, text responses, and abnormal flags. The ObservationGroup (62 cols) and ObservationGroupItem (71 cols) tables provide the structure for multi-item assessment instruments. This generic observation model is how behavioral health EMRs typically store their 50+ assessment tools (PHQ-9, C-SSRS, ASAM, etc.) — each assessment is an ObservationGroup with items as ObservationGroupItems. This is a sound approach that exports the assessment data without hard-coding assessment tool names into the schema.\n\nThe `VisitIntervention` table (33 cols) with goals, objectives, and outcomes captures treatment plan data critical for behavioral health documentation.\n\n**Potential gaps or areas of ambiguity:**\n- **Clinical note full text**: While VisitNote and VisitDocument tables exist, it's unclear whether narrative note content (progress notes, H&P, discharge summaries) is stored as document content or as observations. The `VisitNote.NoteText` (if such a field exists in the 7-column table) or document binary content in `PatientDocument`/`VisitDocument` would contain this. The 7-column VisitNote table may be thin, but clinical notes could be stored as document attachments.\n- **Imaging/radiology reports**: No explicit radiology or imaging table, though results likely flow through the Observation/ObservationSet pathway as they would for lab results.\n- **Scanned documents and attachments**: `NamedImage` (11 cols) and `PatientDocument` tables exist, but it's unclear whether binary document/image content is included in the CSV export or omitted due to format limitations. The `WorkTask.AttachmentData` field is `varbinary`, suggesting binary data is part of the schema.\n\n### Export Format & Standards\n\n**Format**: The export is a **ZIP file containing CSV files** — one CSV per database table. This is a vendor-proprietary format (not FHIR, C-CDA, or any standard), but it is the most appropriate format for a complete database export of this nature.\n\n**Strengths of this approach**:\n- CSV is universally readable and machine-processable\n- One-file-per-table preserves the relational structure\n- The accompanying data dictionary (also CSV) provides complete metadata\n- Foreign key relationships are documented (\"Reference to [TableName]\") allowing reconstruction of table joins\n- Data types and sizes are specified for every column\n- A third party could reconstruct the full database from these exports\n\n**Limitations**:\n- CSV cannot represent binary data (images, scanned documents) — it's unclear how varbinary columns are handled\n- No explicit foreign key constraint definitions beyond the description text\n- No value set documentation for coded fields (e.g., what values are valid for ProblemStatus, ActionCode, etc.)\n- No sample export files are provided to verify the actual CSV structure\n\n**This is genuinely a (b)(10) export, not a repackaged (g)(10)**. The export contains 339 tables covering the entire database — far beyond any FHIR/USCDI subset. It includes billing, pharmacy management, PBM data, work queues, safety rounding, scheduling, and other operational data tied to patient care. This is exactly what a full EHI export should look like.\n\n### Documentation Quality\n\n**Strengths:**\n- The data dictionary is thorough: 339 tables, 3,878 columns, all with data types, sizes, and descriptions\n- The data dictionary is in CSV format (machine-readable) — far better than a PDF\n- Foreign key relationships are explicitly documented\n- The export instructions are clear and actionable\n- The attestation statement is specific about what the export includes\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- The export instructions PDF is a **scanned paper document** — not searchable, not accessible, not version-controllable. This is the weakest element.\n- No sample export files are provided\n- No value set documentation for coded/enumerated fields (what are the valid values for `ProblemStatus`, `OrderStatus`, `ClaimType`, etc.?)\n- Descriptions are generic (\"Problem Code\", \"Action Code\") — they say what the field is but not always what values it takes\n- No explicit ER diagram or relationship diagram showing how tables connect\n- No documentation of which tables correspond to which clinical workflows\n\n**Could a developer implement an import?** Mostly yes. The data dictionary provides enough structural information to create a receiving database schema and load the CSV files. The foreign key references allow reconstruction of relationships. However, interpreting coded values and understanding the clinical semantics of the data would require additional knowledge of the HCS data model.\n\n### Structure & Completeness\n\n- **Granularity**: Field-level documentation with table name, column name, SQL data type, size constraint, and plain-English description for every field\n- **Relationships**: Foreign keys documented via description (\"Reference to [TableName]\")\n- **Data types**: Full SQL type information (bigint, varchar, int, datetime, decimal, bool, varbinary)\n- **Constraints**: Size constraints specified where applicable (e.g., varchar(1000), decimal(15,5))\n- **Value sets**: NOT documented — this is the main gap\n- **Versioning**: The page states \"HCS will update the data dictionary as the database structure evolves with each new version\" but no version history is provided. File last-modified date is 2024-12-30.\n\n## Access Summary\n- Final URL (after redirects): https://www.hcsinc.net/meaningful-use/ (no redirect, same URL)\n- Status: found (but requires browser — curl is blocked)\n- Required browser: yes (site blocks curl/programmatic access with 403)\n- Navigation complexity: direct_link (EHI section is immediately visible on the page with download links)\n- Anti-bot issues: Server returns 403 Forbidden for non-browser HTTP clients. All curl requests (including with realistic User-Agent headers) are blocked. Browser-based access works fine.\n\n## Obstacles & Dead Ends\n\n1. **Anti-bot blocking**: The entire hcsinc.net domain returns 403 Forbidden for curl requests, even with standard User-Agent headers. Content was interpreted from rendered page images.\n\n3. **File URLs use different subdomain**: The links on the page point to `hcsinc.net` (without www), but the site requires `www.hcsinc.net` for browser-context fetches. EHI Export Instructions PDF (2 pages, scanned document)\n\nThe PDF is a scanned paper document (produced by a Konica Minolta bizhub C364e scanner on 2023-12-19), so text extraction yields nothing — the content is only in the page images.\n\n**Page 1** contains:\n- **Product identification**: HCS eMR v10.0\n- **Overview**: Describes a real-time export of all patient information stored in the EHR. The export is available without interacting with HCS Support or Developers. It produces a collection of comma-separated value (CSV) files and a readme file containing a hyperlink to the most up-to-date data dictionary. HCS maintains and updates this documentation as part of their release notes process.\n- **User Access**: The EHI Export function is configurable but defaults to availability for Corporate Users. The \"Corporate User\" authorization role is typically assigned to Administrators and Analysts for EHR at the organization. Organizations use Active Directory to maintain access. The functions are built into HCS eMR at no additional charge and are available autonomously.\n- **Instructions (Creating the Export)**: Users go to System→EHI Export. The menu/screen is the same Patient Selection tool used elsewhere in the application. Users can select a single patient by Visit Identifier, or a group of patients using various filter parameters. After selecting patient(s), users click \"View Patients\" to review the list, then \"Export Patients\" to perform the export.\n\n**Page 2** contains:\n- **Screenshot of the export interface**: Shows the \"Electronic Health Information Export\" screen with extensive filtering options including:\n  - Active in Date Range and Patient Set\n  - Active in Date Range\n  - Active in Patient Set\n  - All Currently Active\n  - Admit Date Range and Patient Set\n  - Admit Date Range\n  - Discharge Date Range and Patient Set\n  - Discharge Date Range\n  - Discharge Date Range and Assigned to Staff\n  - Discharge Date Range and Class\n  - Not Discharged Date Range and Class\n  - Patients with Address in Date Range\n  - Patients with Address in Date Range and Prescriber\n  - Any Entries in Date Range\n  - Patients with Entries in Date Range and Prescriber\n  - Patients with Entries in Date Range\n- **Instructions (Reading the Export)**: The ZIP file exported to the user's \"Downloads\" directory contains a CSV file for each table in the HCS database. The data dictionary describes the data type and size of each field, plus a description of how the field is used and how it relates to other tables. The data dictionary is provided in CSV format for machine readability.\n- **Key statement**: \"The files exported as part of the HCS EHI Export contain all necessary data, including that which is not strictly personal health information, to allow the creation of a complete and fully usable HCS database with only the patient(s) that the users chose to export.\"\n- **Attestation**: Signed by Reubin Felkey (Authorized Representative) on 12/18/2023, stating the documentation is complete with all required elements.\n\n### 2. EHI Data Dictionary CSV (339 tables, 3,878 columns)\n\nThe CSV file has five columns: `Table`, `Column`, `Type`, `Size`, `Description`. It documents every table and column in the HCS database that is included in the EHI export. Each table has a header row (with table name and description) followed by its column definitions.\n\n**Structure**: Tables are separated by blank lines. Each table's first row has only the Table and Description fields filled. Subsequent rows define individual columns with their SQL data types (bigint, varchar, int, datetime, decimal, bool, varbinary, etc.), sizes, and human-readable descriptions. Foreign key relationships are documented as \"Reference to [TableName]\" in the description field.\n\n**Notable tables by domain:**\n\n**Clinical core:**\n- `Patient` (37 cols) — demographics, identifiers, SSN, DOB, gender, ethnicity, language, religion, marital status, veteran status, death info\n- `PatientVisit` (48 cols) — admission/discharge, visit type, class, bed assignment, attending physician, diagnosis info\n- `PatientAllergy` (20 cols) — allergy/intolerance records with severity, reaction, source\n- `PatientDevice` (13 cols) — implantable device tracking (UDI)\n- `PatientDocument` (16 cols) — clinical documents\n- `PatientFamilyHistoryItem` (9 cols) — family history\n- `PatientConsent` (23 cols) — consent documentation\n- `PatientInsuranceCoverage` (27 cols) — insurance/coverage details\n\n**Clinical observations and assessments:**\n- `Observation` (88 cols) — the most detailed observation table with coded values, units, ranges, abnormal flags\n- `ObservationGroup` (62 cols) — observation groupings/panels\n- `ObservationGroupItem` (71 cols) — individual items within observation groups\n- `VisitObservation` (46 cols) — visit-specific observations (vitals, labs, assessments)\n- `VisitObservationSet` (58 cols) — observation sets with specimen collection details\n\n**Diagnoses and problems:**\n- `VisitDiagnosis` (13 cols) — diagnoses with coding system, rank, type\n- `VisitProblem` (19 cols) — problem list with status, classification, evidence, related problems\n- `Condition` (31 cols) — detailed condition records\n\n**Medications and pharmacy:**\n- `PatientOrder` (143 cols) — the largest table, covering all orders including medications, with extensive detail on dosing, frequency, route, prescriber, status, refills, DAW codes, controlled substance info\n- `TherapyAdmin` (45 cols) — medication administration records\n- `AdminProduct` (18 cols) — administered product details (dose, lot, manufacturer, expiration)\n- `HCS_MedList` (27 cols) — medication list entries\n- `MedRecItem` (29 cols) — medication reconciliation items\n- `DispensableProduct`, `RoutedProduct`, `PackagedProduct`, `NamedProduct` — full drug product hierarchy\n\n**Billing and financial:**\n- `VisitCharge` (60 cols) — charges with CPT/HCPCS codes, revenue codes, diagnosis pointers, amounts, modifiers, NDC, service dates, units, expected reimbursement\n- `ChargeClaim` (40 cols) — claim submissions with NCPDP messaging, payer responses, copay info\n- `Payment` (12 cols) — payment records\n- `PatientClaimResponse` (12 cols) — claim responses\n- `CopayProduct`/`CopaySummary` — copay tracking\n- `InsuranceCompany` (24 cols) — insurer master data\n- `InsuranceContract` (9 cols) — contract details\n\n**Care management:**\n- `VisitIntervention` (33 cols) — clinical interventions with goals, objectives, outcomes (treatment plan components)\n- `VisitCarePlan` (4 cols) — care plan records\n- `VisitCareLevel` (7 cols) — level of care tracking\n- `VisitConcern` (8 cols) — patient concerns\n- `ConcernItem` (5 cols) — concern details\n\n**Staff and provider:**\n- `Staff` (80 cols) — provider/staff records with extensive Browser-based access works fine.\n\n## Obstacles & Dead Ends\n\n1. **Anti-bot blocking**: The entire hcsinc.net domain returns 403 Forbidden for curl requests, even with standard User-Agent headers. Files had to be downloaded via browser JavaScript `fetch()` calls and saved through browser DevTools network interception.\n\n2. **PDF is a scan**: The EHI Export Instructions PDF was scanned from a paper document rather than created digitally, making text extraction impossible. Content was interpreted from rendered page images.\n\n3. **File URLs use different subdomain**: The links on the page point to `hcsinc.net` (without www), but the site requires `www.hcsinc.net` for browser-context fetches.
